From creswick at gmail.com  Tue Sep 23 15:25:09 2008
From: creswick at gmail.com (Rogan Creswick)
Date: Tue, 23 Sep 2008 15:25:09 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] How to run fsck on /home partition
In-Reply-To: <48D96951.5020300@comcast.net>
References: <48D96951.5020300@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <c834ec80809231525j3ce5586dv7c32fbca552b785d@mail.gmail.com>

On Tue, Sep 23, 2008 at 3:10 PM, Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net> wrote:
> again. When I did, I got a message telling me to run fsck on /dev/sda3.
> That's /home on my system. fsck warned against running it on a mounted fs.
>

You will need to unmount /home, and the simplest way to do that is
probably to boot up into single-user mode  (I *think* there's an
option in the default grub boot screen to boot into a rescue mode, or
something like that.  If not, you can edit the grub boot line by
poking around in the menu before you select something.  details:
http://www.cyberciti.biz/faq/grub-boot-into-single-user-mode/ )

Once in single user mode, you can check to see if /dev/sda3 is mounted
by running 'mount', and if it is, unmount it:

'umount /dev/sda3'

then fsck it:

'fsck /dev/sda3'

When that finished, just reboot:

'shutdown -r now'


(don't type any of the quotes above, they just delimit the actual commands)

--Rogan

> Do I need to stop X and run from the terminal?
>
> When I tried to umount /home I was told it couldn't be done. I was only
> running a terminal window at the time, but now that I think about it, I
> assume there are some hidden files related to X, or maybe something
> else, that have to be closed.
>
> --
> Regards,
>
> Dick Steffens

From heinlein at madboa.com  Tue Sep 23 15:51:25 2008
From: heinlein at madboa.com (Paul Heinlein)
Date: Tue, 23 Sep 2008 15:51:25 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] How to run fsck on /home partition
In-Reply-To: <c834ec80809231525j3ce5586dv7c32fbca552b785d@mail.gmail.com>
References: <48D96951.5020300@comcast.net>
	<c834ec80809231525j3ce5586dv7c32fbca552b785d@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <alpine.OSX.2.00.0809231548340.24535@guild.galois.com>

On Tue, 23 Sep 2008, Rogan Creswick wrote:

> You will need to unmount /home, and the simplest way to do that is 
> probably to boot up into single-user mode.

That's true enough, and it's certainly the easiest way. If you're 
dying to avoid a reboot,

1. logout as you
2. in a non-X environment, login as root
3. run "lsof /home" to see what processes have open /home files
4. kill said processes
5. umount /home
6. fsck  /home
7. mount /home

-- 
Paul Heinlein <> heinlein at madboa.com <> http://www.madboa.com/

From daehlie at gmail.com  Tue Sep 23 17:57:28 2008
From: daehlie at gmail.com (Kirk Harr)
Date: Tue, 23 Sep 2008 17:57:28 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] How to run fsck on /home partition
In-Reply-To: <c834ec80809231600n4054084ftf90a73d479015eb1@mail.gmail.com>
References: <48D96951.5020300@comcast.net>
	<c834ec80809231525j3ce5586dv7c32fbca552b785d@mail.gmail.com>
	<alpine.OSX.2.00.0809231548340.24535@guild.galois.com>
	<c834ec80809231600n4054084ftf90a73d479015eb1@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <6edf64990809231757u695abc1fja4fd5ebfe4a84108@mail.gmail.com>

I think we are making this more complicated than it needs to be.

mount -o remount,ro /home
fsck -y /home
mount -o remount,rw /home

Problem Solved, no reboots, do not pass go, do not collect $200.

Kirk Harr

From galens at seitzassoc.com  Wed Sep 24 05:20:55 2008
From: galens at seitzassoc.com (Galen Seitz)
Date: Wed, 24 Sep 2008 05:20:55 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] help me understand this pin-level kernel-interface stuff
In-Reply-To: <86tzc6stax.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <86myi4dsi7.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<86abe4c4k6.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>	<c29537840809192241v4b5454b8pae19bc783195441b@mail.gmail.com>	<86d4iy84s9.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
	<86tzc6stax.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <48DA30A7.90101@seitzassoc.com>

Russell Senior wrote:
> Hmm.  Need help parsing this from lspci -vvv:
> 
> 00:0f.0 ISA bridge: Advanced Micro Devices [AMD] CS5536 [Geode companion] ISA (rev 03)
>         Subsystem: Advanced Micro Devices [AMD] CS5536 [Geode companion] ISA
>         Control: I/O+ Mem- BusMaster- SpecCycle+ MemWINV- VGASnoop- ParErr- Stepping- SERR- FastB2B- DisINTx-
>         Status: Cap- 66MHz+ UDF- FastB2B+ ParErr- DEVSEL=medium >TAbort- <TAbort- <MAbort- >SERR- <PERR- INTx-
>         Region 0: I/O ports at 6000 [size=8]
>         Region 1: I/O ports at 6100 [size=256]
>         Region 2: I/O ports at 6200 [size=64]
>         Region 3: I/O ports at 1000 [size=32]
>         Region 4: I/O ports at 9d00 [size=128]
>         Region 5: I/O ports at 9c00 [size=64]
> 
> In particular, what does the "size=foo" mean?  The most likely seems
> to me to be the number of octets available starting at the indicated
> port address.  But other interpretations are possible.  Can anyone
> tell me with some confidence how to interpret the size number?
> 

Size refers to the number of 8 bit locations decoded by the PCI device 
beginning at the given I/O address.  lspci is just telling you how 
each Base Address Register(BAR) is programmed and the size of each 
region.  See section 6.2.5 of the PCI 2.2 spec.  So for Region 0 
above, the device will respond to I/O reads and writes at I/O address 
0x00006000 through 0x00006007.  Note that this does not necessarily 
mean that you can use any size of i/o transaction you want.  For 
example, it could require the use of 8 bit or 16 bit i/o transactions 
to properly access the registers.

The PCI spec is not freely available, but you might want to try 
searching for it anyway.


-- 
Galen Seitz
Seitz & Associates
galens at seitzassoc.com

From heinlein at madboa.com  Wed Sep 24 09:03:16 2008

> On Tue, 23 Sep 2008, Paul Heinlein wrote:
>
>> I don't know. I key roles on folders, not addresses, so I've never really
>> tested that configuration space.

>   "Folder?" Is that a directory?

No, it's a mail folder (aka mailbox). I use Alpine to poll multiple 
inboxes on multiple servers. I use procmail to filter new messages 
into various folders.

The role used in composing and replies is determined by which folder 
is open at the time. If I'm reading mail in my "plug" folder, for 
instance, my madboa.com role becomes the default. For other mailing 
lists, I use my work address.

On Wed, 24 Sep 2008, Rich Shepard wrote:

> On Wed, 24 Sep 2008, Paul Heinlein wrote:
>
>> No, it's a mail folder (aka mailbox).
>
> Paul,
>
>   If I correctly understand, each mbox file is a mail folder/mailbox.

Right. All my mail is mediated by IMAP servers, so I'm not always sure 
about the underlying storage format (it's Maildir in at least one 
place, the one I manage :-) -- but if you're using mbox, then each 
file is a folder/mailbox.

>> I use Alpine to poll multiple inboxes on multiple servers. I use 
>> procmail to filter new messages into various folders.
>
>   Here procmail filters messages from one server into the different 
> folders, but I don't have a separate one for the alternate domain 
> (used only for personal mail).
>
>> The role used in composing and replies is determined by which 
>> folder is open at the time. If I'm reading mail in my "plug" 
>> folder, for instance, my madboa.com role becomes the default. For 
>> other mailing lists, I use my work address.
>
>   Then I need a separate folder for the personal mail that uses the 
> alternate domain and figure out how to specify that in the pine 
> setup.

That's one solution -- and probably the one I'd pick. Keeping mail 
sent to different addresses in different folders seems quite natural 
to me.

The procmail ^TO_ expression makes it quite easy to match the 
recipient address.

Only semi-off-topic: you might give Alpine a try. It's the successor 
to Pine and is quite stable:

   http://www.washington.edu/alpine/

----- Original Message ----
From: Robert Kopp <iconoklastic at yahoo.com>
To: Linux Users <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
Sent: Tuesday, September 23, 2008 1:53:32 PM
Subject: [PLUG] Creative SB X-Fi issues

I installed OpenSuSE 11.0 (x86-64) on a system that has this sound card, and it was not detected. I could not install the beta driver that was made available in April of this year. I understand that this problem also exists with other distros.

Strangely enough, sound does work when Linux is installed as a VMWare image and run on Windows XP, using the same hardware. In this case the driver is snd-ens1371, which cannot be installed in a native Linux installation. 

I'm wondering if anyone knows something more current about this. Some users, of course, have just substituted better-supported hardware for this card.

If you ever do get it working, and you have a 32-bit machine, this is a
worthwhile tweak:

http://groups.google.es/group/earth-linux/browse_thread/thread/e10a5337b0b47ba1#

It not only made the fonts big enough to read, but it made the app
launch faster.

When you run the googleearth.bin installer as a normal user, does it
create a ~/google-earth/ directory, and a symlink ~/googleearth that
points to ~/google-earth/googleearth?  If so, launch it by typing
./googleearth from your home directory.

Carlos

On Tue, Sep 23, 2008 at 7:53 PM, wes <plug at the-wes.com> wrote:
> That still won't work if there is a process with a file open for writing on
> /home.

"lsof /home" will provide the process id of the processes that have
files open in the /home directory, so they can be killed with the kill
command before unmounting the filesystem.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Thu Sep 25 22:16:45 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Thu, 25 Sep 2008 22:16:45 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Scientific Linux at LHC
Message-ID: <20080926051645.GA4012@gate.kl-ic.com>


I run Scientific Linux, which like CentOS is a RedHat Enterprise clone,
customized by Fermilabs for scientific research.  FYI, this went by on
the SL mailing list:

> Christopher Hunter wrote:
> > Out of curiousity, how much of LHC computing is done with scientific linux:
> > - detector event recording (ie. ATLAS) ?
> > - Tier-0 storage backend ?
> > - grid computing ?
> > - (desktop) data analysis

Robert E. Blair wrote:
> Certainly for ATLAS up to tier-0 (and I believe all that follows until a
> user plots a root file on a windows system or linux depending on
> preference and convenience) is all SLC4 (the C is for CERN).  We have
> some windows systems for the slow controls but all analysis/trigger/daq
> including SBCs use SLC4.
> 
> The grid is too, but for all I know some of it may run under XEN or some
> other emulation, so I suppose it could be SL4 under something else.
> 
> - --
> Robert E. Blair, Room E277, Building 362
> Argonne National Laboratory (High Energy Physics Division)

Note that CERN collects 15 petabytes of data per year off the sensors,
and the "interesting" events travel a multi-Gbps pipe over to Argonne
and other labs in the U.S.  So CERN created the web, which created
Linux, which got standardized into SL for science/array usage at
Fermilabs, which runs the Large Hadron Collider experiments at CERN.

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

On Thu, 25 Sep 2008, Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> Date: Thu, 25 Sep 2008 22:04:07 -0700
> From: Richard C. Steffens <rsteff at comcast.net>
> Reply-To: "General Linux/UNIX discussion and help;	civil and on-topic"
>     <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
> To: "General Linux/UNIX discussion and help;	civil and on-topic"
>     <plug at lists.pdxlinux.org>
> Subject: Re: [PLUG] Google Earth in Ubuntu
> 
> Carlos Konstanski wrote:
>> You should take "sudo" out of the equation.  Just install it as a normal
>> user.  Forget the root stuff.
>>
> On one of my attempts I tried that. There were several error messages
> indicating that it was unable to access or create certain directories.
>
> -- 
> Regards,
>
> Dick Steffens

Now that is odd, considering it installs everything in your home
directory.  It makes one directory there called "google-earth", and a
symlink in ~/ that points into there.

Is your user account a local one, or is it a network account (like
Active Directory)?  In other words, does your user account actually
exist in /etc/passwd?

Could there be group membership issues with your user account?  On my
gentoo box, here's what I look like:

ckonstanski at sphinktop:~$ id
uid=1000(ckonstanski) gid=407(ckonstanski)
groups=10(wheel),16(cron),18(audio),27(video),407(ckonstanski),443(plugdev),446(vmware),455(wireshark),456(davfs2)

You certainly don't need all of these to run googleearth, but wheel and
video would be good ones to have, I would think.

And lastly: I have been meaning to try this myself, but haven't gotten
around to it.  What happens if you boot up with knoppix and try to
install googleearth?  This would take the particulars of your distro
installation out of the equation.  You would need enough RAM to run both
knoppix in full GUI mode and the googleearth install, which would
reside in a ramdisk.  You can dramatically decrease the memory footprint
by using a non-KDE desktop.  Here is a page that shows how:

http://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Knowing_Knoppix/Alternatives_to_KDE

If it works in knoppix but not in your installation, then your
installation is somehow suspect.  As you pointed out, it probably has to
do with permissions, either with writing files or accessing system
libraries.  strace would show all reads and writes during the
installation process.  Perhaps this would reveal that you are missing a
required library, or that a library is in an unexpected location (or any
other read/write problem).

I have one geforce2 card in my posession; it is in my server.  I am
reluctant to install googleearth there, but I'll bite the bullet and do
it.  The card is:

nVidia Corporation NV11 [GeForce2 MX/MX 400] (rev b2)

I am running the binary nvidia driver there.  That will have to stay.  I
am using nvidia driver version 96.43.07.  That is a pretty old version.
I have not been able to run a newer one on this box.  It must have to do
with the age of the card itself.

Carlos

Blackboard barely manages to function with optimized defaults, much
less anything that could be vaguely defined as non-standard. Optimized
defaults being Win XP, IE 6, and the latest Java updates. It'll do ok
in OS X as long as you don't try to use Safari, and Vista + IE7 is
it's own special nightmare.

You want actual Java, I'm not sure how Iced, Tea does with it, FireFox
has issues with uploading files in version 3.

amy, who did BlackBoard support at PCC and now for middle and high schools

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Sep 30 03:30:00 2008
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 30 Sep 2008 03:30:00 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] USB Wifi adapters for 64 bit Linux?
Message-ID: <20080930103000.GA21320@gate.kl-ic.com>


I have my sister's laptop back for finishing off.  Got Realplayer,
a few media players, firewall, VMWare, etc. all working with
Ubuntu 8.04 Hardy.

After spending many hours trying to get a Realtek 8187B working
with Ubuntu 8.04 64bit and the default NetworkManager, I gave up
and decided to buy a USB wifi adapter instead.  That way, I can
test it out on my laptop before giving it to her.

The other interfaces on her laptop are Mini PCI Express and Express
Card, both of which have few chipsets with native Linux drivers, and
neither of which I can test on anything but her laptop.  I want to
avoid ndiswrapper if I can.

So, comes the question.  There are quite a few older USB Wifi
adapters out there that are known compatable with Linux, but few
reviews of what is in the stores right now.  I ordered a Trendnet
TEW-424UB 54M G card from Newegg ($10 after rebate) which appears
to work with the zd1211rw driver according to:
   http://linuxwireless.org/en/users/Devices/USB
But of course, the manufacturers like to change the chips without
changing the device model number.   I may be out of luck.

So who has experience with USB Wifi adapters, and has bought one
very recently and got it working with native 64 bit drivers?

Keith

Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs

Hi, I'm an interested linux-using lurker. I think this is my first post to
the list. Greetings! Thanks to all for being so interesting :D

I've just had a couple classes with Blackboard, at PSU, and it worked for me
in Firefox on Ubuntu, even though the "official browser check" on
Blackboard said it was incompatible. Even with that fact, I was able to read
and post to the message boards and use the mail function.

I made sure I was using Sun's Java, which should get easier and easier to do
in Linux because they've GPL'd it. This page will tell you how to easily
specify which Java to use: https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Java

If that doesn't work, I'm not sure what needs to happen for you.

Good luck!

Thanks to doctor juno, chris and others for the suggestions.

When I upgraded Gutsy x86_64 to Hardy x86_64 the dist-upgrade left
Firefox 2 installed. Hence, it was trivial to give it a try. The
results were interesting. First, it crashed on Blackboard the same as
Firefox 3. And Firefox 3 was already running when I launched Firefox 2,
and when Firefox 2 crashed it also crashed Firefox 3. And when I
restarted Firefox 2 the popup "restore previous session" restored both
of them. I'm not sure what to make of that. It doesn't really matter,
because this is the first time I have even launched Firefox 2 since the
upgrade to Hardy. Except for Blackboard, Firefox 3 is totally stable
and does everything. Since Firefox 2 works no better than Firefox 3 on
Blackboard I see no reason to go back to it.

One other interesting thing: When I accessed the Blackboard page
Firefox 2 displayed a message at the top of the window that said I
needed additional plugins to view all the media on the page. When I
told it to install the additional plugins it was Java Runtime
Environment that it wanted to install. Unfortunately, the plugin was
not available. I clicked on the Manual button and it took me to Sun's
download site.

I suspected right from the beginning that the problem was Java.
Unfortunately, I know next to nothing of Java. I left Sun's site until
I figure out which version and module I need. A search in Synaptic on
"java" reveals that I have the following Java things installed:

icedtea-gcjwebplugin
icedtea-java7-jre
icedtea-java7-plugin
java-common
openjdk-6-jre
openjdk-6-jre-headless
openjdk-6-jre-lib
sun-java5-bin
sun-java5-jre
sun-java6-bin
sun-java6-jdk
sun-java6-jre

Lots of other things came up in the search, but those are the only ones
that I thought might be related to the issue.

Further suggestions welcome.

The obvious question is: are you running behind a web proxy?  A packet
trace could verify the quality of the connection.  I cannot remember if
googleearth obeys the environment proxy variables, or if (like the old
IE6 upgrade wizard) you have to wait forever for it to time out before
you have an opportunity to get into the proxy settings.

Looks like My Places is a .kml file in ~/.googleearth.  Also, I see a
lot of these when doing an strace:

stat64("/home/ckonstanski/.config/Google/GoogleEarthPlus.conf", {st_mo
de=S_IFREG|0600, st_size=2313, ...}) = 0

I was not aware that there is a ~/.config/Google directory.  Might want
to delete that, and ~/.googleearth, during the next reinstall.  strace
is handy!

Carlos

On Tue, Sep 30, 2008 at 6:03 PM, John Jason Jordan <johnxj at comcast.net> wrote:
> Firefox 3. And Firefox 3 was already running when I launched Firefox 2,

There is a very good chance you were not actually running firefox 2
(since they crashed at the same time, I'm almost certain you just
spawned another window off of the running firefox 3 install).  It is
not at all easy to start up a separate instance of Firefox if one is
already running.  Without checking the About screen, you may not
notice any difference.

> I suspected right from the beginning that the problem was Java.
> Unfortunately, I know next to nothing of Java. I left Sun's site until
> I figure out which version and module I need. A search in Synaptic on
> "java" reveals that I have the following Java things installed:

For what it is worth, "JNLP" is the Java Network Launch Protocol -- it
has nothing to do with Java*Script*.  JNLP is taking over where
Applets were used in the past.  If you are ever prompted for an
application to open something JNLP related, you probably want to use
'javaws'.

As another aside -- Sun's java is really the only *real* java.  GCJ is
still far, far from complete / stable.

To install the java plugin so you can run applets (which might help
here, it's worth a shot) try this:

First off, in firefox, go to: 'about:plugins' (w/out the quotes) and
look for anything java related, recording what's there if you want, or
just get a feel for what it looks like.

find a file at (or near):

/usr/lib/jvm/java-6-sun-1.6.0.07/jre/plugin/i386/ns7/libjavaplugin_oji.so

The java-6-sun-1.6.0.07 part may be different, but you'll want the
directory in /usr/lib/jvm/ that has the "6" and the "sun" :) if that
matches more than one directory, then take the one with the highest
version number (the 1.6.0.07 part).

Once you've found the libjavaplugin_oji.so, copy it into:

/usr/lib/firefox/plugins/

Restart firefox and go back to 'about:plugins', and see if anything
changed wrt. Java.

Either way, give blackboard a shot and report back :)  (if it still
doesn't work, it would help to know what your about:plugins page says
about java.)

--Rogan
